[FBC/MortgageCompany] mortgage company -- financial service provider that originates and/or funds mortgages for residential or commercial property
[FBC/MotorVehicleLease] motor vehicle lease -- lease of a motor vehicle for a fixed period of time at an agreed amount of money
[FBC/MultilateralTradingFacility] multilateral trading facility -- trading system that facilitates the exchange of financial instruments between multiple parties
[FBC/MutualSavingsBank] mutual savings bank -- financial institution that accepts deposits primarily from individuals and places a large portion of its funds into mortgage loans
[FBC/NationalBank] national bank -- commercial bank whose charter is approved by the Office of the Comptroller of the Currency (OCC) rather than by a state banking agency  Also a subclass of: FBC/CommercialBank, FBC/USBank.
[FBC/NationalInformationCenterControlledVocabulary] National Information Center (NIC) controlled vocabulary -- controlled vocabulary that characterizes some feature or aspect of content about a financial service provider managed in the National Information Center (NIC) repository
[FBC/NegativeAmortization] negative amortization -- amortization in which the payments made do not cover the interest due
[FBC/NegativePledge] negative pledge -- guaranty whereby the issuer will not pledge any assets if doing so would result in less security for lender(s) or investor(s)
[FBC/NegotiableSecurity] negotiable security -- security that can be transferred to another party  Also a subclass of: FND/TransferableContract.
[FBC/NewYorkArticleXIIInvestmentCompany] New York Article XII investment company -- specialized non-depository lending institution that has broad borrowing and lending powers and may invest in stocks and bonds
[FBC/NICEntityTypeClassifier] National Information Center (NIC) entity type classifier -- controlled vocabulary and codes for describing the nature of the functional entities managed by the National Information Center (NIC) repository
[FBC/NICRegistryEntry] National Information Center (NIC) registry entry -- an entry in the the National Information Center (NIC) repository, a repository of financial data and institution characteristics collected by the Federal Reserve System
[FBC/NonBankSubsidiaryOfADomesticEntity] non-bank subsidiary of a domestic entity -- non-bank entity of which 25 percent or more of whose voting shares are owned or controlled by an entity that is based in the United States, or of which a majority of its directors are controlled by such domestic entity, or of which 25 percent or more of whose voting shares are held by trustees for the benefit of the shareholders or members of such domestic entity
[FBC/NonDepositoryInstitution] non-depository institution -- financial institution that does not have a full banking license and typically is not supervised by a national or international banking regulatory agency
[FBC/NonDepositoryTrustCompany] non-depository trust company -- trust company that accepts and executes trusts, but does not issue currency; non-depository trust companies can either be Federal Reserve Members or Federal Reserve Non-members  Also a subclass of: FBC/TrustCompany.
[FBC/NonDepositoryTrustCompany-MemberInstitution] non-depository trust company - member institution -- non-depository trust company that is a member of the Federal Reserve system  Also a subclass of: FBC/FederalReserveSystemMember.
[FBC/NonDepositoryTrustCompany-NonMemberInstitution] non-depository trust company - non-member institution -- non-depository trust company that is not a member of the Federal Reserve system
[FBC/NonEuropeanEconomicAreaBranch] non European Economic Area branch -- a branch of a credit institution whose Head Office is in a third country
[FBC/NonNegotiableSecurity] non-negotiable security -- security that is not transferable to another party
[FBC/NonPhysicalCollateral] non-physical collateral -- asset pledged as collateral that is a financial asset, rather than physical asset
[FBC/NonTransactionDepositAccount] non-transaction deposit account -- any deposit account that is not explicitly considered a transaction account
[FBC/NorthAmericanIndustryClassificationSystemCode] North American Industry Classification System code -- the North American Industry Classification System (NAICS) code representing an industry
[FBC/NorthAmericanIndustryClassificationSystemScheme] North American Industry Classification System scheme -- the scheme defining the North American Industry Classification System (NAICS) Codes
[FBC/ObligationAcceleration] obligation acceleration -- credit event triggered when one or more reference obligations become immediately due and payable as a result of a default or covenant breach on the reference entity's other debt instruments, subject to a materiality threshold
[FBC/ObligationDefault] obligation default -- credit event triggered as a result of an obligation-specific default  Also a subclass of: FBC/ObligationSpecificCreditEvent.
[FBC/ObligationRestructuring] obligation restructuring -- credit event that materially impacts an obligation, such as an interest rate reduction, principal reduction, deferral of interest or principal, change in priority ranking, or change in currency or composition of payment
[FBC/ObligationSpecificCreditEvent] obligation-specific credit event -- credit event that relates to an individual credit agreement or debt instrument (reference obligation)  Also a subclass of: DER/TriggeringEvent.
[FBC/Offeree] offeree -- party that receives an offer from something from someone (i.e., an offerer) based on the terms of the offering
[FBC/Offering] offering -- expression of interest in providing something to someone that is contingent upon acceptance, forbearance, or some other consideration, as might be desired by an offeree(s)
[FBC/Offeror] offeror -- party that proposes to make something available to someone (i.e., an offeree) based on the terms of the offering
[FBC/OfferPrice] offer price -- price suggested by a prospective seller at a particular time for a given security
[FBC/OfficeOfAForeignBank] office of a foreign bank -- facility that is any branch, agency, representative office, or commercial lending company subsidiary of a foreign bank in the United States
[FBC/OfficialClosingPrice] official closing price -- price of the final trade of a security at the end of a trading day on a given exchange
[FBC/OffMarketFacility] off-market facility -- facility used for reporting over-the-counter (OTC) and other direct trades that are not executed by the exchange but are reported through the exchange
[FBC/OpenDate] open date -- date on which something was created
[FBC/OpeningPrice] opening price -- price at which something first trades at the start of a trading day
[FBC/OperatingLevelMarket] operating-level market -- exchange/market/trade reporting facility in a specific market/country
[FBC/OperatingLevelMarketIdentifier] operating-level market identifier -- market identifier that identifies an exchange/market/trade reporting facility in a specific market/country
[FBC/Option] option -- derivative instrument that grants to the holder either the privilege to purchase or the privilege to sell the assets specified at a predetermined price or formula at or within a time period in the future
[FBC/OrganizationCreditRating] organization credit rating -- credit rating that provides an opinion of creditworthiness of an organization
[FBC/OrganizedTradingFacility] organised trading facility -- multi-lateral system which is not an RM or an MTF and in which multiple third-party buying and selling interests in bonds, structured finance products, emission allowances or derivatives are able to interact in the system in a way that results in a contract in accordance with the provisions of Title II of MiFID II
[FBC/PackagedFinancialProduct] packaged financial product -- financial product that acts as a container for at least one financial instrument, including other financial products, and whose value is derived from, or based on a reference asset, market measure, or investment strategy  Also a subclass of: FND/ContractualProduct.
[FBC/PartialAmortization] partial amortization -- amortization in which the very last payment the last payment due may be a large balloon payment of all remaining principal and interest
[FBC/PaymentDueDate] payment due date -- date by which payment of the current outstanding balance, part thereof, or a minimum amount due must be made to the creditor
[FBC/PaymentInstitution] payment institution -- a legal person that has been granted authorisation in accordance with Article 10 to provide and execute payment services throughout the European community
[FBC/PaymentService] payment service -- financial service that involves acceptance of electronic payments by a variety of payment methods including credit card, bank-based payments such as direct debit, bank transfer, and real-time bank transfer based on online banking
[FBC/PayrollDeductionsProgramNumber] payroll deductions program number -- concatenation of an entity's business number, the 'RP' abbreviation and a 4-digit subaccount number used for reporting payroll deductions
[FBC/PayrollService] payroll service -- financial service, typically provided to small businesses that are not large enough to have an internal finance organization, that involves managing payment of wages to employees
[FBC/PhysicalCollateral] physical collateral -- asset pledged as collateral that has a material form, i.e., is a physical asset of the obligor
[FBC/PhysicalSettlementTerms] physical settlement terms -- commitment to deliver the actual underlying asset on the specified delivery date, rather than cash
[FBC/Policyholder] policyholder -- counterparty to and typically owner of an insurance policy
[FBC/Position] position -- investor's stake, i.e., a holding, in a particular asset (such as an individual security)
[FBC/PostingDate] posting date -- date that determines in which posting period a document or journal entry is added to an account record
[FBC/PriceAnalytic] price analytic -- statistical measure involving security prices
[FBC/PriceDeterminationMethod] price determination method -- strategy for calculating or otherwise establishing a price for something
[FBC/PriceSpread] price spread -- difference between two prices
[FBC/PricingModel] pricing model -- expression used to determine a value for an instrument at a given point in time
[FBC/PrimaryFederalRegulator] primary federal regulator -- federal regulatory agency that is designated as the main agency responsible for oversight of a given institution for an institution
[FBC/Principal] principal -- with respect to a debt: the value of an obligation, such as a bond or loan, raised and that must be repaid at maturity; for investments: the original amount of money invested, separate from any associated interest, dividends or capital gains
[FBC/PrincipalPayment] principal payment -- event reflecting the actual payment of some amount of the principal of a debt
[FBC/PrincipalPaymentSchedule] principal payment schedule -- regular, contract-specific schedule including the dates on which some percentage or all of the principal is due to be (re)paid  Also a subclass of: FND/PaymentSchedule.
[FBC/PrincipalRepaymentTerms] principal repayment terms -- contract terms that specify requirements for repayment of the principal
[FBC/PrincipalUnderwriter] principal underwriter -- underwriter who, as principal, purchases from an investment company, or pursuant to some contract has the right to purchase from such company, any security for distribution, or who as agent for such company sells or has the right to sell any security to a dealer or to the public, excluding any dealer who purchases from such company through sn underwriter acting as an agent for such company
[FBC/PriorityLevel] priority level -- relative ranking that a guaranty has in the context of a contract, for example for a credit enhancement priority
[FBC/ProductLifecycle] product lifecycle -- lifecycle specific to a product or product family
[FBC/ProductLifecycleEvent] product lifecycle event -- kind of event that occurs during one or more stages of a product lifecycle
[FBC/ProductLifecycleEventOccurrence] product lifecycle event occurrence -- actual occurrence of an event that happens during a specific stage of a specific product lifecycle
[FBC/ProductLifecycleOccurrence] product lifecycle occurrence -- realization of the lifecycle of a specific product
[FBC/ProductLifecycleStage] product lifecycle stage -- phase in a product lifecycle
[FBC/ProductLifecycleStageOccurrence] product lifecycle stage occurrence -- realization of a specific stage in the lifecycle of a given product
[FBC/ProjectedContractEventSchedule] projected contract event schedule -- schedule of events, including but not limited to anticipated payment events, rate reset events and others that are expected to occur over the lifetime of the contract
[FBC/PromissoryNote] promissory note -- debt instrument that is a written promise by one party to another that commits that party to pay a specified sum on demand or within a specified time frame under specified terms
[FBC/QuoteDrivenMarket] quote-driven market -- exchange in which prices are determined from bid and ask quotations made by market makers, dealers, or specialists
[FBC/RateOfReturn] rate of return -- net gain or loss on an investment over a specified time period, expressed as a percentage of the investment's initial cost or value as of a specific point in time
[FBC/RateResetTimeOfDay] rate reset time of day -- time of day that an interest rate is reset, as indicated by some interest rate authority or market data provider
[FBC/RecognizedMarketOperator] recognised market operator -- exchange that is operated or maintained by an operator registered under certain securities regulations that brings together purchasers and sellers of capital market products
[FBC/RedemptionProvision] redemption provision -- contract provision enabling the issuer (writer) to regain possession through repayment of some stipulated price
[FBC/RegionalAdministrativeOfficeOfAForeignBank] regional administrative office of a foreign bank -- representative office that  (1) Is established by a foreign bank that operates two or more branches, agencies, commercial lending companies, or banks in the United States;  (2) Is located in the same city as one or more of the foreign bank's branches, agencies, commercial lending companies, or banks in the United States;  (3) Manages, supervises, or coordinates the operations of the foreign bank or its affiliates, if any, in a particular geographic area that includes the United States or a region thereof, including by exercising credit approval authority in that area pursuant to written standards, credit policies, and procedures established by the foreign bank; and  (4) Does not solicit business from actual or potential customers of the foreign bank or its affiliates.
[FBC/RegisteredAgent] registered agent -- legal agent designated by some party to represent them and act on their behalf under a formal agency agreement  Also a subclass of: FND/ContractParty.
[FBC/RegisteredCharityProgramNumber] registered charity program number -- concatenation of an entity's business number, the 'RR' abbreviation and a 4-digit subaccount number used for registered charity contribution
[FBC/RegisteredInvestmentAdvisor] registered investment advisor -- registered agent and financial service provider that advises high net worth individuals on investments and manages their portfolios  Also a subclass of: FBC/RegisteredAgent.
[FBC/RegisteredMultilateralTradingFacility] registered multilateral trading facility -- multilateral system operated by an investment firm or market operator, which brings together multiple third-party buying and selling interests in financial instruments in the system, in accordance with non-discretionary rules, in a way that results in a contract in accordance with the provisions of Title II of the MiFID II
[FBC/RegistrationAuthorityCode] registration authority code -- identifier that uniquely identifies a business registry, and is associated with a registration authority and jurisdiction, issued by the Global Legal Entity Identifier Foundation (GLEIF)
[FBC/RegistrationStatus] registration status -- lifecycle stage indicating the status of a given registration of something, such as a business or legal entity, as specified by the registration authority
[FBC/RegulatedCommodity] regulated commodity -- commodity under the jurisdiction of the regulatory agency, such as the Commodities Futures Trading Commission (CFTF) in the United States, which includes any commodity traded in an organized contracts market
[FBC/RegulatedExchange] regulated exchange -- regulated market that is operated by and/or managed by a market operator that brings together or facilitates the bringing together of multiple third-party buying and selling interests in financial instruments
[FBC/RegulationIdentificationScheme] regulation identification scheme -- a scheme for organizing information and allocating identifiers to regulations
[FBC/RegulationIdentifier] regulation identifier -- an identifier associated with a regulation
[FBC/RegulatoryCapacity] regulatory capacity -- the capacity of some natural person to regulate some industry, organization, or product by virtue of some certification program on behalf of some regulatory agency
[FBC/RelationshipManager] relationship manager -- responsible party who manages a client's account and oversees their relationship with the service provider
[FBC/RepresentativeOfficeOfAForeignBank] representative office of a foreign bank -- office of a foreign bank which is located in any state and is not a federal branch, federal agency, state branch, state agency, or commercial lending company subsidiary
[FBC/Repudiation] repudiation -- credit event involving the refusal to honor the terms of a contract
[FBC/ResearchStatisticsSupervisionDiscountIdentifier] Research, Statistics, Supervision and Regulation, and Discount and Credit identifier -- unique identifier assigned by the Federal Reserve to financial institutions for regulatory and oversight purposes
[FBC/RetailCreditFacility] retail credit facility -- credit facility that is a loan or line of credit used by retailers and real estate companies
[FBC/RevolvingLineOfCredit] revolving line of credit -- credit facility that enables the borrower to withdraw funds, repay, and withdraw again
[FBC/RiskPoolingInstitution] risk pooling institution -- financial institution that provides some financial service while spreading the financial risk inherent in that service to lower the probability of a catastrophic financial event by aggregating customers across diverse dimensions as a risk management practice
[FBC/RoutingTransitNumber] routing transit number -- unique nine digit identifier, used primarily in the United States, to identify a banking or other financial institution for clearing funds, and, as it appears on a check, denotes the banking institution that holds the account from which funds are to be drawn
[FBC/SalesFinanceCompany] sales finance company -- finance company that purchases retail and wholesale paper from automobile and other consumer and commercial goods dealers
[FBC/SavingsAssociation] savings association -- depository institution that is (a) any federal savings bank or association chartered under section 1464 of the Federal Deposit Insurance Act; (b) any state chartered building and loan association, savings and loan association, or homestead association; or (c) any cooperative bank (other than a cooperative bank which is a state bank as defined in subsection (a)(2)) of the Federal Deposit Insurance Act, which is organized and operating according to the laws of the State (as defined in subsection (a)(3)) in which it is chartered or organized; and (c) any corporation (other than a bank) that the board of directors and the comptroller of the currency jointly determine to be operating in substantially the same manner as such a depository institution
[FBC/SavingsBank] savings bank -- banking institution organized to accept savings deposits and pay interest on those savings deposits
[FBC/SavingsLoanAssociation] savings loan association -- financial institution that accepts deposits primarily from individuals and channels its funds primarily into residential mortgage loans
[FBC/SavingsLoanHoldingCompany] savings loan holding company -- company that directly or indirectly controls a savings association or related holding company, and explicitly excludes any company that is also a bank holding company  Also a subclass of: FBC/FinancialServiceProvider.
[FBC/SecuritiesTransaction] securities transaction -- transaction between two or more parties involving the exchange of commonly defined financial products
[FBC/Security] security -- financial instrument that can be bought or sold
[FBC/SecurityAgreement] security agreement -- collateral agreement that grants a financial interest in some collateral to a party that is not an owner of that collateral, specifying terms including relative duties and rights, over and above those specified in the primary contract, regarding the disposition of the asset used as collateral
[FBC/SecurityPrice] security price -- monetary price for a financial instrument at some point in time
[FBC/SelfRegulatingOrganization] self-regulating organization -- non-governmental organization that has the power to create and exercise some degree of regulatory authority over an industry or profession in some country or group of countries
[FBC/Settlement] settlement -- act of finalizing a transaction, including but not limited to finalizing accounting, exchanging consideration, and/or legally recording documents, as applicable
[FBC/SettlementConvention] settlement convention -- convention employed to determine the closing date (from the stated settlement date) in the process of settling a transaction on which securities or interests in securities are delivered, usually against (in simultaneous exchange for) payment of some consideration
[FBC/SettlementEvent] settlement event -- specific event involving the finalization a transaction or portion thereof, including but not limited to finalizing accounting, exchanging consideration, and/or legally recording documents, as applicable
[FBC/SettlementTerms] settlement terms -- contract terms that define the commitment to and mechanism for settling one or more sides of a transaction
[FBC/ShortTermCreditRating] short term credit rating -- credit rating that provides an opinion of the probability of an individual or organization going into default within a year
[FBC/SoftCreditEvent] soft credit event -- default event that is repairable
[FBC/SpotContract] spot contract -- financial instrument that settles for immediate delivery on a specified date
[FBC/StandardIndustrialClassificationCode] standard industrial classification code -- the SIC code representing an industry
[FBC/StandardIndustrialClassificationScheme] standard industrial classification scheme -- the scheme defining the Standard Industrial Classification (SIC) Code List
[FBC/StandardizedTerms] standardized terms -- contract terms that, grouped together, that are generally and consistently reused across many contracts, published by some organization, and capable of being incorporated into a contract by reference
[FBC/StateAgencyOfForeignBankingOrganization] state agency of foreign banking organization -- agency of a foreign bank established and operating under the laws of any state, where state means any State of the United States or the District of Columbia
[FBC/StateBranchOfForeignBankingOrganization] state branch of foreign banking organization -- branch of a foreign bank located in any State of the United States at which deposits are received, established and operating under the laws of that State, where state means any State of the United States or the District of Columbia
[FBC/StateCharteredBank] state-chartered bank -- commercial bank whose charter is approved by a state banking regulator  Also a subclass of: FBC/USBank.
[FBC/StateCreditUnion] state credit union -- credit union that has a state affiliation
[FBC/StateGovernmentEntity] state government entity or agency -- formal organization that is an independent agency, instrumentality or other permanent or semi-permanent organization in the machinery of government of any one of the states or territories of the United States
[FBC/StateMemberBank] state member bank -- state-chartered bank that is a member of the Federal Reserve System (FRS)  Also a subclass of: FBC/FederalReserveSystemMember.
[FBC/StateSavingsBank] state savings bank -- savings bank that has a state affiliation
[FBC/SubFacility] sub-facility -- portion of a credit facility extended to the borrower for some purpose, possibly per some schedule specified in the facility
[FBC/SubsidiaryOfADomesticEntity] subsidiary of a domestic entity -- entity of which 25 percent or more of whose voting shares are owned or controlled by an entity that is based in the United States, or of which a majority of its directors are controlled by such domestic entity, or of which 25 percent or more of whose voting shares are held by trustees for the benefit of the shareholders or members of such domestic entity
[FBC/SwapExecutionFacility] swap execution facility -- exchange that enables participants to execute and trade swaps
[FBC/SystematicInternaliser] systematic internaliser -- investment firm that, on an organised, frequent, systematic and substantial basis, deals on its own account by executing client orders outside a regulated exchange, MTF or OTF without operating a multilateral system
[FBC/TaxAuthority] tax authority -- regulatory agency that has jurisdiction over the assessment, determination, collection, imposition and other aspects of any tax
[FBC/TaxpayerIdentificationNumber] taxpayer identification number -- identification number used by the Internal Revenue Service (IRS) in the administration of tax laws in the United States
[FBC/TaxpayerIdentificationNumberingScheme] taxpayer identification numbering scheme -- tax identification scheme used in the United States
[FBC/ThirdPartyAgent] third-party agent -- any service provider that is licensed to perform a legally binding function and has been legally empowered to act on behalf of another party  Also a subclass of: FND/Licensee.
[FBC/ThriftInstitution] thrift institution -- savings association that primarily accepts savings account deposits and invests most of the proceeds in mortgages  Also a subclass of: FBC/DomesticEntity.
[FBC/TimeCertificateOfDepositAccount] time certificate of deposit account -- time deposit account that allows deposits evidenced by a negotiable or nonnegotiable instrument, or a deposit in book entry form evidenced by a receipt or similar acknowledgement issued by the bank, that provides, on its face, that the amount of such deposit is payable to the bearer, to any specified person, or to the order of a specified person, as follows: (1) on a certain date not less than seven days after the date of deposit, (2) at the expiration of a specified period not less than seven days after the date of the deposit, or (3) upon written notice to the bank which is to be given not less than seven days before the date of withdrawal.
[FBC/TimeDepositAccount] time deposit account -- deposit account that the depositor does not have a right, and is not permitted, to make withdrawals from within six days after the date of deposit unless the deposit is subject to an early withdrawal penalty of at least seven days' simple interest on amounts withdrawn within the first six days after deposit  Also a subclass of: FND/ContractualProduct.
[FBC/TimeDepositOpenAccount] time deposit open account -- time deposit account that allows deposits (other than time certificates of deposit) for which there is in force a written contract with the depositor that neither the whole nor any part of such deposit may be withdrawn prior to (1) the date of maturity, which shall be not less than seven days after the date of the deposit, or (2) the expiration of a specified period of written notice of not less than seven days
[FBC/Trade] trade -- situation that realizes an agreement between parties participating in a voluntary action of buying and selling goods and services
[FBC/TradeIdentifier] trade identifier -- sequence of characters identifying a trade within some context
[FBC/TradeLifecycle] trade lifecycle -- lifecycle that defines the evolution of a trade, from initiation through settlement
[FBC/TradeLifecycleEvent] trade lifecycle event -- kind of event that occurs during one or more stages of the lifecycle of a trade
[FBC/TradeLifecycleEventOccurrence] trade lifecycle event occurrence -- realization of an event that happens during a specific stage of a specific trade lifecycle
[FBC/TradeLifecycleOccurrence] trade lifecycle occurrence -- realization of the lifecycle for a specific trade
[FBC/TradeLifecycleStage] trade lifecycle stage -- phase in the lifecycle of a trade
[FBC/TradeLifecycleStageOccurrence] trade lifecycle stage occurrence -- realization of a phase in the lifecycle of a specific trade
[FBC/Trader] trader -- party that engages in the transfer of financial assets in any financial market on behalf of a client or the financial services provider
[FBC/TradeReportingFacility] trade reporting facility -- facility that provides a mechanism for the reporting of transactions effected otherwise than on an exchange
[FBC/TradingDay] trading day -- time span that a particular trading venue is open
[FBC/TradingSession] trading session -- window of time within a trading day in which orders may be placed and filled
[FBC/TradingStrategy] trading strategy -- approach used for buying and selling in the securities markets
[FBC/TransactionCategory] transaction category -- high-level classifier for an individual transaction
[FBC/TransactionDate] transaction date -- date on which a specific transaction was initiated
[FBC/TransactionDepositAccount] transaction deposit account -- deposit account from which the depositor / account holder is permitted to make transfers or withdrawals by negotiable / transferable instruments, payment orders of withdrawal, telephone transfers, and so forth, and that may be accessible via an electronic device such as an automated teller machine (ATM), remote service unit (RSU), mobile device, and by debit card
[FBC/TransactionIdentifier] transaction identifier -- identifier for an individual transaction associated with an account
[FBC/TransactionRecord] transaction record -- record of transactions associated with an account

[IND/CurrencyConversionService] currency conversion service -- foreign exchange service involving the conversion of currency of one country or group of countries for another, typically, but not always, as a counter transaction
[IND/CurrencyForwardRate] currency forward rate -- rate of exchange between two currencies for settlement at some future point in time, expressed as a premium on the spot rate
[IND/CurrencyForwardRateVolatility] currency forward rate volatility -- measure of exchange rate fluctuation based on a range of projected values for exchange rates  Also a subclass of: IND/ImpliedVolatility.
[IND/CurrencySpotBuyRate] currency spot buy rate -- indicative spot buying market rate as observed by the reporting source
[IND/CurrencySpotMidRate] currency spot mid rate -- indicative middle market (mean of spot buying and selling) rate as observed by the reporting source
[IND/CurrencySpotRate] currency spot rate -- rate at which one currency may be exchanged for another for immediate delivery
[IND/CurrencySpotSellRate] currency spot sell rate -- indicative spot selling market rate as observed by the reporting source
[IND/CurrencySpotVolatility] currency spot volatility -- measure of exchange rate fluctuation based on a range of past actual values for exchange rates  Also a subclass of: IND/HistoricalVolatility.
[IND/CurrentEmploymentStatistics] current employment statistics -- survey conducted on a regular basis that presents analytical information related to businesses and government agencies, in order to provide detailed industry data on employment, hours, and earnings of workers
[IND/CurrentPopulationSurvey] current population survey -- survey conducted on a regular basis that presents analytical information related to the general population of a given statistical area with respect to labor force, employment, unemployment, persons not in the labor force, hours of work, earnings, and other demographic and labor force characteristics
[IND/DailyAverageMarketRate] daily average market rate -- overall level of a given rate, calculated as the sum of some selected observed values of the rates for a particular reference rate, foreign exchange rate, lending rate, or other market rate divided by the number of samples collected over the course of a twenty-four (24) hour period for a specific date
[IND/DiscouragedWorkerPopulation] discouraged worker population -- subset of the marginally attached population that have given a job-market related reason for not currently looking for work
[IND/EconomicIndicator] economic indicator -- statistical measure of economic activity that is regular and comparable in the context of a statistical area (region), used for analysis of economic performance and predictions of future performance
[IND/EmployedPopulation] employed population -- subset of the civilian labor force considered to be employed during the reporting period
[IND/EmployedPopulationPartTime] employed population part-time -- subset of the employed population that includes persons that are working fewer than 30 to 35 hours per week based on usual working hours
[IND/EmployedPopulationPartTimeForEconomicReasons] employed population part-time for economic reasons -- subset of the employed population that includes persons that are working fewer than 30 to 35 hours per week due to slack work, unfavorable business conditions, inability to find full-time work, and seasonal declines in demand  Also a subclass of: IND/UnderemployedPopulation.
[IND/EmployedPopulationPartTimeForNonEconomicReasons] employed population part-time for non-economic reasons -- subset of the employed population that includes persons that are working fewer than 30 to 35 hours per week due to illness or other health or medical limitations, childcare problems, family or personal obligations, being in school or training, retirement or Social Security limits on earnings, and having a job where full-time work is less than 35 hours
[IND/EmployedPopulationTemporarilyNotAtWork] employed population temporarily not at work -- subset of the employed population that includes persons that are temporarily absent from work for various reasons
[IND/EmploymentPopulationRatio] employment-population ratio -- economic indicator representing the ratio of the employed population with respect to the overall civilian non-institutional population of a given economy for some specified period
[IND/EmploymentSituationEstablishmentSurvey] employment situation establishment survey -- survey conducted on a regular basis that presents analytical information related to the labor force of a given statistical area, surveyed with respect to businesses, and is, for the most part, seasonally adjusted
[IND/EmploymentSituationHouseholdSurvey] employment situation household survey -- a survey conducted on a regular basis that presents analytical information related to the labor force of a given statistical area, surveyed with respect to households, and is, for the most part, seasonally adjusted
[IND/EmploymentSituationSurvey] employment situation survey -- a survey conducted on a regular basis that presents analytical information focused on the employment characteristics of a given statistical area  Also a subclass of: IND/CurrentPopulationSurvey.
[IND/EndOfDayMarketRate] end-of-day market rate -- value of a given market rate of the end of the business day for a specific date
[IND/Enterprise] enterprise -- functional business entity that produces and/or sells goods or services  Also a subclass of: IND/InstitutionalUnit.
[IND/EnterprisePopulation] enterprise population -- statistical universe consisting of enterprises designed for the purposes of supporting surveys such as those used as the basis for employment and producer price indices
[IND/EquityIndex] equity index -- benchmark whose constituents are exclusively equity instruments
[IND/Establishment] establishment -- an enterprise (or part of an enterprise) that operates from a single physical location
[IND/EstablishmentEmployment] establishment employment -- economic indicator representing the total number of persons who work in or for the establishment including working proprietors, active business partners and unpaid family workers, as well as persons working outside the establishment when paid by and under the control of the establishment, for example, sales representatives, outside service engineers and repair and maintenance personnel
[IND/EstablishmentPopulation] establishment population -- a subset of the enterprise population focused on establishments
[IND/ExchangeRateStructure] exchange rate structure -- structured collection of quoted or projected exchange rates, such that volatility may be constructed for the structure
[IND/ExchangeRateVolatility] exchange rate volatility -- statistical measure of the rate of change in the rate at which one currency can be exchanged for another
[IND/FixedBasket] fixed basket -- basket of goods and services whose quantity and quality are held fixed for some period of time  Also a subclass of: FND/DatedStructuredCollection.
[IND/FixedBasketConstituent] fixed basket constituent -- component of a fixed basket  Also a subclass of: FND/DatedCollectionConstituent.
[IND/FixedBasketPopulation] fixed basket population -- statistical universe consisting of specific goods and/or services designed for the purposes of supporting surveys such as those used as the basis for price indices
[IND/ForeignExchangeService] foreign exchange service -- financial service involving the exchange of one currency for another, conversion of one currency for another, and transfer of money from one country to another whereby currency conversion is required
[IND/GovernmentSpecifiedStatisticalArea] government-specified statistical area -- statistical area defined by a government agency
[IND/GrossDomesticProduct] gross domestic product -- economic indicator representing the broadest measure of aggregate economic activity, measuring the total unduplicated market value of all final goods and services produced within a statistical area in a period
[IND/HistoricalPriceVolatility] historical price volatility -- historical volatility measure of past trading ranges of prices of underlying securities and indexes  Also a subclass of: IND/PriceVolatility.
[IND/HistoricalVolatility] historical volatility -- measure of volatility that uses actual values for pricing, rates, and other measurements calculated over some prior period
[IND/Household] household -- individual or small group of persons who occupy a housing unit (such as a house or apartment) as their usual place of residence, who pool some, or all, of their income and wealth and who consume certain types of goods and services collectively, mainly housing and food
[IND/HousingUnit] housing unit -- house, an apartment, a mobile home or trailer, a group of rooms, or a single room occupied as separate living quarters, or if vacant, intended for occupancy as separate living quarters
[IND/ImpliedPriceVolatility] implied price volatility -- measure of volatility that represents the expected fluctuations of an underlying stock or index over a specific time frame  Also a subclass of: IND/PriceVolatility.
[IND/ImpliedVolatility] implied volatility -- measure of volatility that is a forward-looking metric used to calculate probability
[IND/IndustrialProductsSector] industrial products sector -- a classifier for a sector of the economy used for price indices focused on major commodities sold by manufacturers in Canada
[IND/InflationRate] inflation rate -- economic indicator representing a change in prices of goods and services for a specified period, for a given statistical area
[IND/InputProducerPriceIndex] input producer price index -- economic indicator representing measure of the rate of change over time in the prices of inputs of goods and services purchased by the producer
[IND/InstitutionalPerson] institutional person -- person that resides in an institution for some reason, due, for example, to hospitalization, rehabilitation, or incarceration
[IND/InstitutionalUnit] institutional unit -- party that is capable, in its own right, of owning assets, incurring liabilities, and engaging in economic activities and in transactions with other parties
[IND/InterbankBidRate] interbank bid rate -- interbank rate that is the interest rate at which participating banks are willing to borrow deposits from other banks

[IND/InterbankOfferedRate] interbank offered rate -- interbank rate that is the interest rate at which participating banks lend money
[IND/InterbankRate] interbank rate -- reference rate that is the rate of interest charged on short-term loans between banks

[IND/MarginallyAttachedPopulation] marginally attached population -- subset of the population that includes people who currently are neither working nor looking for work but indicate that they want and are available for a job and have looked for work sometime in the past 12 months
[IND/MarketCapitalization] market capitalization -- expression representing the perceived value of a company as determined by the stock market at a specific point in time

[IND/MarketSpread] market spread -- statistical measure providing the difference (or spread) between two market rates

[IND/MicropolitanStatisticalArea] micropolitan statistical area -- one or more adjacent counties or county equivalents that have at least one urban core area of at least 10,000 population but less than 50,000, plus adjacent territory that has a high degree of social and economic integration with the core as measured by commuting ties
[IND/MilitaryPerson] military person -- person that is a member of the active duty military

[IND/PriceVolatility] price volatility -- statistical measure of the rate of change in pricing for a given security or market index
[IND/ProducerPriceIndex] producer price index -- economic indicator representing measure of the rate of change over time in the prices of goods and services bought and sold by producers
[IND/Productivity] productivity -- economic indicator representing ratio of a volume measure of output to a volume measure of input use
[IND/QuotedExchangeRate] quoted exchange rate -- exchange rate quoted at a specific point in time, for a given block amount of currency as quoted against another (base) currency  Also a subclass of: IND/MarketRate.
[IND/QuotedPrice] quoted price -- a monetary price quoted by some publisher on a given date

[IND/ReferenceIndex] reference index -- measure of change in the value of the contents of a basket over a given period of time
[IND/ReferenceInterestRate] reference interest rate -- market rate that is a rate of interest paid by or agreed among some bank or set of banks  Also a subclass of: IND/MarketRate.

[IND/StatisticalInformationPublisher] statistical information publisher -- publisher that packages and makes analytical and statistical data available

[IND/UltimateConsumer] ultimate consumer -- person that is the ultimate user of a good, product or service
[IND/UnderemployedPopulation] underemployed population -- subset of the employed population that includes persons employed part-time for economic reasons, who want and are available for full-time work but have had to settle for a part-time schedule
[IND/UnderemployedPopulationWithRespectToOccupation] underemployed population with respect to occupation -- subset of the underemployed population that includes persons employed in a role that does not reflect their training and experience, excluding those that change careers
[IND/UnderutilizedPopulation] underutilized population -- subset of the civilian non-institutional population that includes persons employed part-time for economic reasons, persons that are marginally attached to the labor force, and persons that are identified as unemployed
[IND/UnemployedPopulation] unemployed population -- subset of the civilian labor force that is considered to have had no employment but was available for work, except for temporary illness, and had made specific efforts to find employment sometime during a specified period, during the reporting period
[IND/UnemploymentRate] unemployment rate -- economic indicator representing the ratio of the unemployed population with respect to the civilian labor force of a given economy for some specified period

[IND/Volatility] volatility -- statistical measure of the dispersion around the average of some random variable over some period of time

[LOAN/LenderRight] lender right -- Rights on the lender to protect them against loss. furthe rNtoes: Logically, considering the two parties, they both have protecxtion mechanisms. so while the lender has protecxtion mechanisms through mortgage insurance, and the consumer has protextion mechanisms such as good faith estimates. also the agencies (see Consumer Protection Agency), an instance of which is the CFPB in the US (just set up). Lender rights are: - expressed in the Contract Consumer protection develops becaues the contract is written by the potential Lender. So the rights are introcued to rectify the imbalance between the two parties. Same goes for insurance. consumer protection laws (governe dby the relevant consumer protection agency. So the lender protexts itself as it writes th contract AND does the things it needs to do to protext itself, but on the approval process, and with later instruments such as insurance. Interestingly., it is the Borrower who pays for this by paying for credit reports etc. So the borrower protects itself by other mechanisms. Caveat emptor - displaced by regulation (the buyer is protected by regulation). Uberimae Fidae - in the utmost good faith. Mortgage Insurance is an additional means of mitigating the risk, that the lended may have., so if the information assessed is not accurate, or if the borrower's situation changes for the worse. then the risk rating may go down. So the Mortgage Insurance is a further strategy which mitigates any shortfall in the Lender Righrs that you may have - ie someone guarantees. In the US you can also avoid that by having paid a deposit. PIMI: Principal, Interst and Morgage Insurance. So the Borrower pays towards the MI, esxcept if they have paid a given amount as deposit. there are 2 types of MI: 1. protects the lender in the event of borrower degault 2. Insurance for "Incapacity to pay the mortage" (these can be bought off the shelf - can combine health, unemployment etc.). - this is the Borrower mitigating their own risk. Prevents foreclosure. Similar to general sickness etc. Where the lender charges for MI, the cost is passed onto the Borrower. e.g. if there is a % valuation (e.g. 70% in Aus, 80% in US for example) then no insurance is required.

Dealing with default, helping borrowers make payment Collections Default admin Foreclosure Reselling All dealt with by several sub departments. This requires subject matter experts in this area. 1. scoping Identify default as a possible state. This hands off to other business processes. Once you get into the default scenario we are talking about a proces that is going to fall into place over a period of time. The bank works out what to do with the default scenario, e.g. whether it restructures, forecloses, seeks restitution from the security (collateral). It does nto help us to understand the structure of the loan, rather tha consequences of the loan. If we were to further explore the default detail we would bring in other SMEs. And we would have to model a process flow. 1.1 impact on the pool of an MBS Loan Default Proceeding (special ase of legal thing) is an aspect of Default Management / Administratoin. there is also the State of the Loan. Sale / something / fulfilment / fiunduing / approved = servicing mode. Something happens (non payment) =&gt; Default Grace Period followed by negotiation. Some threshold whereby after a given amount of delinquency it needs to go into some other process moving towards foreclosure. Do State Diagram. Stages of loan.

[LOAN/LoanPurpose] loan purpose -- A selection of different types of loan purpose, being the purpose for which and manner in which loan (credit) draw-down amounts are to be used. This shows the purpose for which credit is to be used, and implies certain kinds of fact that relate to that specific type of loan e.g. mortgages. These are also identified as tranche types in tranches of a credit facility.

[LOAN/LoanToValueRatio] loan-to-value ratio -- ratio, expressed as a percentage, between the principal amount of the loan and the appraised value of the asset securing the financing
[LOAN/MagneticStripeVerificationCodeValue] magnetic stripe verification code or value -- card verification code on a card's magnetic stripe that uses secure cryptographic processes to protect data integrity on the stripe, and reveals any alteration or counterfeiting

[LOAN/MortgageIndemnityGuarantee] mortgage indemnity guarantee -- insurance-backed guarantee that protects lenders if the mortgage repayments cease for some reason, perhaps due to death or a homeowner being made redundant at work
[LOAN/MortgageIndemnityGuarantor] mortgage indemnity guarantor -- guarantor and insurer that provides mortgage insurance in the form of a mortgage indemnity guarantee (MIG)  Also a subclass of: FBC/Insurer.

[SEC/AgencyJumpTranche] agency jump tranche -- A tranche where if there is some sort of trigger event reached then the holders of the tranche will begin to receive payments.
[SEC/AgencyJumpZTranche] agency jump z tranche -- A Jump Z tranche is like a Z tranche but if there is some sort of trigger event reached then the holders of the Jump Z tranche will begin to receive payments. Regular non-Sticky Jump Z tranches maintain their changed status only while the trigger event is in effect, and revert to their old payment status once the trigger event has passed.  Also a subclass of: SEC/AgencyZTranche.

[SEC/AgencyRegularJumpZ] agency regular jump z -- Regular non-Sticky Jump Z tranches maintain their changed status only while the trigger event is in effect, and revert to their old payment status once the trigger event has passed.
[SEC/AgencyStickyJumpZ] agency sticky jump z -- "Sticky" Jump Z tranches maintain the payment priority of a Jump Z tranche until they are retired.
[SEC/AgencyZTranche] agency z tranche -- A tranche that does not receive payments while other tranches remain.

[SEC/AmortizingBond] amortizing bond -- bond that regularly pays down the principal (face value) on the debt along with its interest expense over the life of the bond
[SEC/ArbitrageCDO] arbitrage c d o -- Arbitrage CDO/CLO/CBO - the reference assets are bought by a firm or conduit or SPV (Special Purpose Vehicle) with a view to repackage them and sell them on as the structured product.
[SEC/ArbitrageCdoObjective] arbitrage cdo objective -- The objective is arbitrage, whereby the motivation is to add value by repackaging assets into tranches.
[SEC/ArbitrageSyntheticCDO] arbitrage synthetic c d o -- Arbitrage synthetic CDO deals are motivated by regulatory or practical considerations that might make a bank want to retain ownership of debt while achieving capital relief through CDSs. In this case, the sponsoring bank has a portfolio of obligations, called the reference portfolio. It retains that portfolio, but offloads its credit risk by transacting CDSs with the CDO.  Also a subclass of: SEC/SyntheticCDO.
[SEC/AssetBackedSecurity] asset-backed security -- debt instrument backed by receivables other than those arising out of real estate loans or mortgages

[SEC/AssetClassStrategy] asset class strategy -- Strategy which is asset class based.
[SEC/AttachmentPoint] attachment point -- lower tranche boundary of a tranche defined as a percentage of the value of the total pool of collateral, either at issuance or as of some point in time
[SEC/AuctionDateRule] auction date rule -- business recurrence interval convention that is a published rule for defining the date of some auction event
[SEC/AuctionRateDividend] auction rate dividend -- preferred share dividend whose rate is periodically reset through an auction, typically every 7, 14, 28, or 35 days

[SEC/BermudanExerciseTerms] Bermudan exercise terms -- exercise terms that stipulate that an option may only be exercised on predetermined dates within some exercise window, often on one day each month or at the date of expiration
[SEC/BestEffortsOffering] best efforts offering -- securities offering whereby investment bankers commit to doing their best to sell the securities offered, but do not assume the full risk of an underwriter
[SEC/BillOfExchange] bill of exchange -- short-term negotiable financial instrument consisting of an order in writing addressed by one person (the seller of goods) to another (the buyer), requiring the latter to pay a fixed amount of money on demand (a sight draft) or on a predetermined date (a time draft)
[SEC/BlueSkyLaw] blue sky law -- state-level securities regulation, designed to protect investors against securities fraud that require issuers to be registered and to disclose details of their offerings

[SEC/CashflowCDO] cashflow c d o -- A cash-flow CDO is analogous to a CMO. Cash flows from collateral are used to pay principal and interest to investors. If such cash flows prove inadequate, principal and interest is paid to tranches according to seniority. At any point in time, all immediate obligations to a given tranch are met before any payments are made to less senior tranches.
[SEC/CashflowStructure] cashflow structure -- The source of funds for the CDO is cashflow. this means that cash flows from collateral are used to pay principal and interest to investors.
[SEC/CDOCashflowTreatmentStructure] c d o cashflow treatment structure -- The way in which cash flows are handled in a CDO.

[SEC/CollateralizedBondObligation] collateralized bond obligation -- structured debt security that has investment-grade bonds as its underlying assets backed by the receivables on high-yield or junk bonds
[SEC/CollateralizedDebtObligation] collateralized debt obligation -- structured finance constructed from a portfolio of fixed income assets including corporate loans and mortgage backed securities. A special purpose vehicle (SPV) issues notes to investors in order to raise funds that are invested in a portfolio of those fixed income assets, held by the SPV as collateral for the notes. Further notes: Collateralized Debt Obligation, for example, ABS CDO which consists of a portfolio of different ABS bonds, and the payments to the holders of these trust certificates are derived from the cash flows of the ABS bonds. This CDO instrument is part of a CDO issue, consisting of individual CDO instruments of a given seniority. Often referred to as tranches and slices (Investopedia). Investopedia: Similar in structure to a collateralized mortgage obligation (CMO) or collateralized bond obligation (CBO), CDOs are unique in that they represent different types of debt and credit risk. In the case of CDOs, these different types of debt are often referred to as 'tranches' or 'slices'. Each slice has a different maturity and risk associated with it. The higher the risk, the more the CDO pays. Further details: Collateralized Debt obligations are securitized interests in pools of - generally non-mortgage - assets. Assets - called collateral - usually comprise loans or debt instruments. A CDO may be called a collateralized loan obligation (CLO) or collateralized bond obligation (CBO) if it holds only loans or bonds, respectively. Investors bear the credit risk of the collateral. Multiple tranches of securities are issued by the CDO, offering investors various maturity and credit risk characteristics.

[SEC/FundsProcessingAccount] funds processing account -- An account used specifically in the processing of funds. Like all accounts this is (per FIBIM definition) a business relationship between two entities; one entity is the account owner, the other entity is the account servicer. Please refer to Financial global model for treatment of accounts relationships in this model.
[SEC/FundsProcessingParty] funds processing party -- party involved in the processing of funds
[SEC/FundSubscriptionTerms] fund subscription terms -- Subscription terms for the fund. Further notes: ISO FIBIM, EFAMA DD and FPP combine terms for subscription, redemption and general holding requirements. These have been separated here as they are different kinds of term, but this can be reviewed. Subscription Terms are identified as terms of the fund and not the fund unit, since terms for how you might subscribe can't be binding one someone who has not yet subscribed.

[SEC/IssuedDebt] issued debt -- debt that is set out by the borrower in some form of financial security in which the lender is the holder or counterparty of that security

[SEC/JumpZTriggerEvent] jump z trigger event -- The event which triggers the Jump Z
[SEC/JumpZTriggerEventReversal] jump z trigger event reversal -- The reversal of the event which triggers the Jump Z
[SEC/JurisdictionStrategy] jurisdiction strategy -- Strategy which is jurisdiction based.
[SEC/KeyInvestorInformationDocument] key investor information document -- short document that provides critical information for investors, summarizing content derived from a prospectus such that it can be understood by investors without reference to other documents, as required by law in the European Union
[SEC/LastRegularCouponDate] last regular coupon date -- scheduled date of the last regular coupon payment, that is the last of the payments that are made according to a regular repeating series of coupon periods, before any non-standard (long or short) final coupon period in the schedule
[SEC/LeadArranger] lead arranger -- financial institution that spearheads the loan structuring and syndication process on behalf of the borrower
[SEC/LegalFundStructure] legal fund structure -- structure of a fund with respect to its legal formation in some jurisdiction
[SEC/LegalHoldingRestriction] legal holding restriction -- security restriction applicable to holding the security
[SEC/LimitedPartnershipUnit] limited partnership unit -- share in a form of partnership similar to a general partnership, except that in addition to one or more general partners (GPs), there are one or more limited partners (LPs)
[SEC/ListedBond] listed bond -- bond that may be traded on an exchange  Also a subclass of: SEC/ListedSecurity.
[SEC/ListedSecurity] listed security -- registered security listed on at least one exchange
[SEC/ListedSecurityIdentifier] listed security identifier -- security identifier issued in the public domain and referred to in listings and other relevant publications
[SEC/ListedShare] listed share -- share that is listed on at least one platform  Also a subclass of: SEC/ListedSecurity.
[SEC/Listing] listing -- catalog entry for a securities offering managed by an exchange that provides the terms under which that security is made available on that exchange
[SEC/ListingService] listing service -- service provided by an exchange to facilitate securities trading
[SEC/LoanParticipationNote] loan participation note -- credit facility and fixed-income security that may be distributed across a group of lenders  Also a subclass of: LOAN/CommercialLoan, SEC/FixedIncomeSecurity.
[SEC/LoanPool] loan pool -- debt pool whose consituents are loans
[SEC/LuxembourgDepositaryReceipt] Luxembourg depositary receipt -- global depositary receipt that represents the purchase, or ownership, of foreign assets which are deposited in a Luxembourg-based account
[SEC/MakeWholeCall] make whole call -- call allowing the issuer to pay off remaining debt early
[SEC/MakeWholeFeature] make whole feature -- a call provision allowing the issuer to pay off remaining debt early
[SEC/ManagedCDO] managed c d o -- A CDO where the reference assets are bought (the portfolio is ramped up) and then the CDO manager may alter the portfolio as they see fit.
[SEC/ManagedCDOPortfolio] managed c d o portfolio -- A portfolio where the reference assets of the CDO are bought (the portfolio is ramped up) and then the CDO manager may alter the portfolio as they see fit.
[SEC/ManagedInvestment] managed investment -- investment pool that is controlled by a professional investment manager who invests the pool in various financial instruments and assets that align with their investment objectives and is overseen by a board of directors
[SEC/ManagedManagementStyle] managed management style
[SEC/MandatoryConvertibleBond] mandatory convertible bond -- convertible bond that converts into shares at maturity regardless of the equity price
[SEC/Margin] margin -- a variable that is added to a specified index rate to determine the fully indexed interest rate charged to a borrower on a credit balance
[SEC/MarketValueCDO] market value c d o
[SEC/MarketValueStructure] market value structure
[SEC/MBSInstrumentSlice] m b s instrument slice -- A holding of an individual slice or slices of a tranche.
[SEC/MBSIssuer] m b s issuer -- The issuer of a Mortgage Backed Security.
[SEC/MBSPool] m b s pool -- A pool investment consisting of a collection of MBS instruments.
[SEC/MBSTrancheNote] m b s tranche note -- An individual note of a tranche.
[SEC/MediumTermNote] medium term note -- bond issued over time under a shelf registration program, where each issue may have a different coupon and maturity typically ranging from one to ten years
[SEC/MezzanineCDOTranche] mezzanine c d o tranche -- The tranche between senior and subordinated. Mezzanine tranches of a CDO issue are typically rated B to BBB.
[SEC/MezzanineMBSTranche] mezzanine m b s tranche -- Specific kinds of tranche are modeled for example and investigation only and have been removed from the diagrams. These will be removed from the final model.
[SEC/MiFIDRegulatedSecurity] MiFID regulated security -- security for which MiFID reporting is required
[SEC/MixedBasket] mixed basket -- basket that has a mix of constituents, including securities and indices  Also a subclass of: FND/DatedStructuredCollection.
[SEC/MoneyMarketInstrument] money market instrument -- a short-term debt security that gives the owner the unconditional right to receive a stated, fixed sum of money on a specified date
[SEC/MortgageBackedSecurity] mortgage-backed security -- debt obligations that represent claims to the cash flows from pools of mortgage loans, most commonly on residential property
[SEC/MortgageBackedSecurityOfferingProspectus] mortgage-backed security offering prospectus -- Prospectus describing the terms of the issue and each of the instruments included in the mortgage backed security issue. Term origin:SMER
[SEC/MortgagePool] mortgage pool -- loan pool consisting of mortgages that are held in trust as collateral for the issuance of a mortgage-backed security
[SEC/MunicipalBond] municipal bond -- government bond that may be issued by a regional, rather than national, authority  Also a subclass of: SEC/MunicipalSecurity.
[SEC/MunicipalDebtFundsUsage] municipal debt funds usage -- official statement specifying how the funds raised via a new issue of municipal securities are to be applied
[SEC/MunicipalDebtRemarketingAgent] municipal debt remarketing agent -- municipal securities dealer responsible for reselling to investors securities (such as variable rate demand obligations and other tender option bonds) that have been tendered for purchase by their owner  Also a subclass of: FND/ContractThirdParty.
[SEC/MunicipalDebtSourceOfFunds] municipal debt source of funds -- official statement identifying the source of funds for a new issue of municipal securities
[SEC/MunicipalNote] municipal note -- short-term obligation to repay a specified principal amount on a certain date, together with interest at a stated rate, usually payable from a defined source of anticipated revenues
[SEC/MunicipalSecurity] municipal security -- debt obligation issued by a regional governmental entity
[SEC/MunicipalTrustee] municipal trustee -- financial institution with trust powers, designated by the issuer, that acts, pursuant to a bond contract, in a fiduciary capacity for the benefit of the bondholders in enforcing the terms of the bond contract  Also a subclass of: FBC/FinancialInstitution.
[SEC/MutualFund] mutual fund -- open-end professionally managed investment fund established for the purpose of investing in securities such as stocks, bonds, money market instruments and similar assets
[SEC/NationalNumberingAgency] national numbering agency -- registration authority responsible for issuing and managing National Securities Identifying Numbers for securities in accordance with the ISO 6166 standard in some jurisdiction (typically that of a country)
[SEC/NationalSecuritiesIdentifyingNumber] National Securities Identifying Number -- generic, nine-digit alpha numeric code which identifies a fungible security, assigned by a national numbering agency under the ISO 6166 standard
[SEC/NationalSecuritiesIdentifyingNumberRegistry] National Securities Identifying Number registry -- registry used by a national numbering agency to manage the financial instrument identifiers and related information that it registers
[SEC/NationalSecuritiesIdentifyingNumberRegistryEntry] national numbering agency registry entry -- entry in a National Securities Identifying Number registry
[SEC/NationalSecurityIdentificationScheme] national security identification scheme -- security identification scheme, defining the format and structure of a National Securities Identifying Number (NSIN), published nationally on behalf of a country
[SEC/NetAssetValueCalculationMethod] net asset value calculation method -- Parameters for the calculation of the net asset value for an investment fund/fund class.
[SEC/NilPaidShare] nil paid share -- share whose payment status indicates that none of the market value has been received by the company for the shares
[SEC/NonAgencyIOTranche] non agency i o tranche -- Interest Only tranche, meaning that this tranche will only pay interest.
[SEC/NonAgencyJumpTranche] non agency jump tranche -- A tranche where if there is some sort of trigger event reached then the holders of the tranche will begin to receive payments.
[SEC/NonAgencyJumpZTranche] non agency jump z tranche -- A Jump Z tranche is like a Z tranche but if there is some sort of trigger event reached then the holders of the Jump Z tranche will begin to receive payments. Regular non-Sticky Jump Z tranches maintain their changed status only while the trigger event is in effect, and revert to their old payment status once the trigger event has passed.  Also a subclass of: SEC/NonAgencyZTranche.
[SEC/NonAgencyMBSIssuer] non agency m b s issuer -- A party which is a non agency issuer of MBS securities. The identity of this party may be a bank or a specialist (non agency) mortgage company. Term origin:MBS PoC Reviews
[SEC/NonAgencyMortgagePool] non agency mortgage pool
[SEC/NonAgencyPOTranche] non agency p o tranche -- Principal Only tranche. This tranche will only pay principal.
[SEC/NonAgencyRegularJumpZTranche] non agency regular jump z tranche -- Regular non-Sticky Jump Z tranches maintain their changed status only while the trigger event is in effect, and revert to their old payment status once the trigger event has passed.
[SEC/NonAgencyStickyJumpZTranche] non agency sticky jump z tranche -- "Sticky" Jump Z tranches maintain the payment priority of a Jump Z tranche until they are retired.
[SEC/NonAgencyZTranche] non agency z tranche -- A tranche that does not receive payments while other tranches remain.
[SEC/NonCumulativePreferredShare] non-cumulative preferred share -- preferred share whose dividend payments are not carried forward
[SEC/NonParticipatingPreferredShare] non-participating preferred share -- preferred share that is not a participating preferred share
[SEC/NonprofitFund] nonprofit fund -- investment vehicle designed to support a nonprofit mission, whose objectives include environmental stewardship and/or social responsibility in addition to financial performance
[SEC/NonTradableDebtInstrument] non-tradable debt instrument -- a debt instrument that may not be bought or sold  Also a subclass of: FND/WrittenContract.
[SEC/NonTradableFundUnit] non-tradable fund unit -- security representing an interest in a fund that cannot be traded ontside of the fund itself  Also a subclass of: SEC/FundUnit.
[SEC/NonVotingShare] non-voting share -- share that has no voting right
[SEC/NoteFund] note fund -- pooled investment vehicle that issues debt instruments (notes) to investors rather than (or in addition to) traditional equity interests
[SEC/NoteFundShare] note fund share -- investment interest in a fund that issues notes rather than traditional equity, in cases where the fund is structured as a company
[SEC/NoteFundUnit] note fund unit -- investment interest in a fund that issues notes rather than traditional equity, in cases where the fund is structured as a trust, partnership, or unitized fund
[SEC/NotificationProvision] notification provision -- provision of a redemption feature defining notification requirements
[SEC/OfferingDocument] offering document -- legal document that states the objectives, risks and terms of an investment
[SEC/OfferingStatement] offering statement -- offering memorandum that conforms to Regulation A, Offering Statement, of the Securities Act of 1933
[SEC/OffshoreDepositaryReceipt] offshore depositary receipt -- depositary receipt issued under SEC Regulation S
[SEC/OpenEndInvestment] open-end investment -- investment fund that offered through a fund company that sells shares directly to investors
[SEC/OrdinaryDividend] ordinary dividend -- dividend that is paid to shareholders periodically
[SEC/OrganizationStrategy] organization strategy -- Strategy which is organization based.
[SEC/OriginalIssueDiscountBond] original issue discount bond -- interest-bearing bond issued at a deep discount to face value
[SEC/OtherInvestmentFundInformation] other investment fund information -- Things which are not part of the prospectus but are important if you want to understand the fund.
[SEC/PAC-1Class] p a c-1 class -- Planned Amortization Class tranche. PAC-1 is the most senior Planned Amortization Class tranche.
[SEC/PAC-2Class] p a c-2 class -- Planned Amortization Class tranche. PAC-2 refers to a support tranche that is given a scheduled payment structure like a PAC bond.
[SEC/PAC-3Class] p a c-3 class -- Planned Amortization Class tranche. Additional support tranche with scheduled payments.
[SEC/PACPOTranche] p a c p o tranche -- Planned Amortization Class principal only tranche.  Also a subclass of: SEC/PlannedAmortizationClassBond.
[SEC/PACTrancheAmortizationSchedule] p a c tranche amortization schedule
[SEC/PAC-ZTranche] p a c- z tranche -- Planned Amortization Class tranche which is also a Z tranche, that is Definition needed.  Also a subclass of: SEC/PlannedAmortizationClassBond.
[SEC/PartialCall] partial call -- call of part of an issue
[SEC/PartialCallFeature] partial call feature -- call feature whereby the issuer can recall part of the issue on scheduled dates, where bonds are selected to be called according to some rule, or by selecting various bonds at random
[SEC/PartiallyPaidShare] partially paid share -- share whose payment status indicates that only a portion of the market value has been received by the company for the shares
[SEC/PartialRedemptionAllocationConvention] partial redemption allocation convention -- convention used to determine how the partial call will be actioned with respect to bond selection
[SEC/ParticipatingPreferredShare] participating preferred share -- preferred share that, in addition to paying a stipulated dividend, gives the holder the right to participate with common share holders in additional distributions of earnings under specified conditions
[SEC/ParticipatoryNote] participatory note -- tradable debt instrument that facilitates the ownership of securities traded in other jurisdictions  Also a subclass of: SEC/DepositaryReceipt.
[SEC/PassThroughMBSDeal] pass through m b s deal -- An issue of Mortgage Backed Security instruments in which payments on the pool are passed through to investors
[SEC/PassThroughMBSDealProspectus] pass through m b s deal prospectus -- The written prospectus for an agency, pass through issue of Mortgage Backed Securities
[SEC/PassThroughMBSInstrument] pass through m b s instrument -- A security in which the cash flows from the underlying asset pool are passed through to the investor by way of redemption payments.
[SEC/PassThroughMBSInstrumentNote] pass through m b s instrument note -- An individual note of a pass through instrument.
[SEC/PassThroughMBSIssueUnderwriter] pass through m b s issue underwriter -- The party which agrees to buy any certificates that are not bought by investors Term origin:MBS PoC Reviews
[SEC/Pass-throughPool] pass-through pool
[SEC/PayingAgent] paying agent
[SEC/PensionFund] pension fund -- investment fund run by a financial intermediary on behalf of an organization and its employees/members
[SEC/PerpetualBond] perpetual bond -- bond that has no maturity date, i.e., one that pays interest in perpetuity
[SEC/PerpetualPreferredShare] perpetual preferred share -- preferred share that has no fixed maturity date
[SEC/PlannedAmortizationClassBond] planned amortization class bond -- Planned Amortization Class tranche.This is a tranche where the principal payment must follow a certain schedule.
[SEC/Pool] pool -- combination of resources for a common purpose or benefit
[SEC/PoolBackedSecurity] pool-backed security -- debt instrument that derives its cashflow from an underlying pool of mortgage loans or other receivables
[SEC/PoolConstituent] pool constituent -- component of a pool
[SEC/PooledFund] pooled fund -- pool of funds that a group of investors combines for common benefit  Also a subclass of: FND/FinancialAsset.

[SEC/PortfolioHolding] PortfolioHolding
[SEC/PortfolioInvestmentStrategy] portfolio investment strategy -- The manner in which the portfolio manager tries to reach the funds objectives.
[SEC/PrecedenceRight] precedence right -- right that give the shareholder higher priority with respect to certain pre-defined dividend payments over other shareholders and that pay out first in the case of liquidation
[SEC/PreferredDividend] preferred dividend -- commitment to distribute a portion of earnings to shareholders, similar to a dividend but often with a fixed payment amount and schedule

[SEC/PreferredShare] preferred share -- share that pays dividends at a specified rate and has preference over common shares in the payment of dividends and liquidation of corporate assets
[SEC/PreferredShareInFund] preferred share in fund
[SEC/PreferredShareWithAdjustableRateDividend] preferred share with adjustable rate dividend -- preferred share whose dividend rate varies according to some benchmark
[SEC/PreferredShareWithAuctionRateDividend] preferred share with auction rate dividend -- preferred share whose dividend rate is periodically reset through an auction, such as a Dutch auction
[SEC/PreferredShareWithFixedMaturityDate] preferred share with fixed maturity date -- preferred share whose maturity date is set, typically according to the terms of the prospectus
[SEC/PreferredShareWithFixedRateDividend] preferred share with fixed rate dividend -- preferred share whose dividends are set, typically according to the terms of the prospectus
[SEC/PreferredVotingExchangeableAdjustableIncomeRegisteredShare] preferred, voting, exchangeable, adjustable income, registered share -- preferred share that confers exactly one vote per share, may be exchanged for securities of another issuer, provides a periodic income whose dividend rate is set periodically, and is registered  Also a subclass of: SEC/PreferredShareWithAdjustableRateDividend, SEC/SingleVotingShare, SEC/RegisteredSecurity.
[SEC/PreferredVotingExchangeableAuctionRateIncomeRegisteredShare] preferred, voting, exchangeable, auction rate income, registered share -- preferred share that confers exactly one vote per share, may be exchanged for securities of another issuer, provides a periodic income whose dividend rate is adjusted through an auction, and is registered  Also a subclass of: SEC/PreferredShareWithAuctionRateDividend, SEC/SingleVotingShare, SEC/RegisteredSecurity.

[SEC/PrescriptiveEvent] prescriptive event -- event related to the imposition or enforcement of a rule, method, formula, etc.
[SEC/PricePerShare] price per share -- price for one share of a given security at some point in time  Also a subclass of: FND/UnitPrice.
[SEC/PrincipalOnlyStrip] principal-only strip -- a strip that represents the principal portion of the monthly payments on the underlying debt instrument, such as a bond
